Introduction
The Every Angle API provides an easy way to integrate your Every Angle data in Airtable with any external system. The API closely follows REST semantics, uses JSON to encode objects, and relies on standard HTTP codes to signal operation outcomes.

The API documentation below is specifically generated for your base. We recommend that you use the graphical Airtable interface to add a few records of example data for each table. These records will be displayed in the documentation examples generated below.

To view documentation for all available endpoints, as well as documentation that has not been generated specific to your base, please visit here.

The ID of this base is appZXteLrpESv7H8X.

Please note: if you make changes to a field (column) name or type, the API interface for those fields will change correspondingly. Therefore, please make sure to update your API implementation accordingly whenever you make changes to your Airtable schema from the graphical interface.

Official API client:

JavaScript: airtable.js (Node.js + browser)
Community-built API clients:

Ruby: airrecord
.NET: airtable.net
Python 3: pyairtable
Python 2/3: airtable.py
Metadata
This API gives you the ability to list all of your bases, tables, fields, and views. For more, see the API reference documentation for List bases and Get base schema.

Rate Limits
The API is limited to 5 requests per second per base. If you exceed this rate, you will receive a 429 status code and will need to wait 30 seconds before subsequent requests will succeed.

The official JavaScript client has built-in retry logic.

If you anticipate a higher read volume, we recommend using a caching proxy. This rate limit is the same for all plans and increased limits are not currently available.

Authentication
Airtable uses simple token-based authentication. For personal development, we recommend using personal access tokens, which can be created at /create/tokens. To learn more about other authentication methods like OAuth, please visit our developer documentation.

Using Airtable.js in the browser is strongly discouraged, since that will expose your API key to everyone who has access to that web page.

To configure Airtable.js either store your secret API token (e.g. personal access token) in the AIRTABLE_API_KEY environment variable or pass it directly to the client library. Note that environment variables are not available when using Airtable.js in the browser.

All API requests must be authenticated and made over HTTPS.

 
Example using environment variable
# Shell:
$ export AIRTABLE_API_KEY=YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN

# Node:
const base = require('airtable').base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');
Example using custom configuration
var Airtable = require('airtable');
Airtable.configure({
    endpointUrl: 'https://api.airtable.com',
    apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'
});
var base = Airtable.base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');
Gigs Table
The id for Gigs is tbldxbkHiZOEcpkrk. Table ids and table names can be used interchangeably in API requests. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

Fields
Each record in the Gigs table contains the following fields:

Field names and field ids can be used interchangeably. Using field ids means field name changes do not require modifications to your API request. We recommend using field ids over field names where possible, to reduce modifications to your API request if the user changes the field name later.

List Gigs records
To list records in Gigs, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Performer Fee (actual), pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Performer Fee (actual)"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldFY7TZkaqgMy9CC", "fldLxflIepPzkTRwA"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Gigs table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gigs').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Play:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Play"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved 01/01/20 - DO NOT DELETE - 
Retrieved 17/05/24 - Jessica Bramwell - 50 Washington St, Glasgow G3 8AZ
Retrieved 06/06/24 - Kirsten McQuillan - Blair Drummond Safari and Adventure Park, Blair Drummond, Stirling
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Gigs').select({
    view: 'Play'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Gigs').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Gigs record
To retrieve an existing record in Gigs table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

In attachment objects included in the retrieved record (Invoices and other documents), only id, url, and filename are always returned. Other attachment properties may not be included. Note: Attachment URLs returned will expire 2 hours after being returned from our API. If you want to persist the attachments, we recommend downloading them instead of saving the URL. See our support article for more information.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gigs').find('recHk3FbcTQHAvU2v', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recHk3FbcTQHAvU2v
Create Gigs records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

To create new attachments in Invoices and other documents, set the field value to an array of attachment objects. When creating an attachment, url is required, and filename is optional. Airtable will download the file at the given url and keep its own copy of it. All other attachment object properties will be generated server-side soon afterward.

Note that in most cases the API does not currently return an error code for failed attachment object creation given attachment uploading happens in an asynchronous manner, such cases will manifest with the attachment object either being cleared from the cell or persisted with generated URLs that return error responses when queried. If the same attachment URL fails to upload multiple times in a short time interval then * the API may return an ATTACHMENTS_FAILED_UPLOADING error code in the details field of the response and the attachment object will * be cleared from the cell synchronously.

We also require URLs used to upload have the https:// or http:// protocol (Note: http:// support will be removed in the near future), have a limit of 3 max redirects, and a file size limit of 1GB. In addition, URLs must be publicly accessible, in cases where cookie authentication or logging in to access the file is required, the login page HTML will be downloaded instead of the file.

Attachment URLs returned will expire 2 hours after being returned from our API. If you want to persist the attachments, we recommend downloading them instead of saving the URL.

If too many attachments are uploaded within a short period of time, the server may return a partial failure on record creation with an "Attachment Upload Rate Too High" error. See our support article for more information.

Values for Name, Performer Fee (actual), GOTO emails, Profit (theoretical), Profit (theoretical/current), Balance Amount, Amount Paid (Turnover), Amount Paid (current), options_ids, Options Price, Options Fees, Description (from event), Early Arrival Price, Late Finish Price, Subtotal, Discount Applied, Date (from event), Total Due (calculated), Deposit Due (Calculated), Profit (projected), Profit (Pot), is_done, Name (from Performers), fillout - song selection, Formatted Date, _has_band?, _has_video, _has_photo, _has_dj, set list (favourites), set list (must-play), set list (avoid), amount (from Gig Payment), _quote_options, Quote, Karaoke (cost), Songs (from Set List Items), Set List Duration (seconds), Set List Total Duration, set list built (copyable), fillout - gig details, GOTO interface, Profit (current) and Profit (theoretical/pot) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

Update Gigs records
To update Gigs records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Gigs records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To add attachments to Invoices and other documents, add new attachment objects to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing attachment objects that you wish to retain, to keep preexisting attachments providing id is required (which can be retrieved using the retrieve endpoint), other fields are ignored. For the new attachments being added, url is required, and filename is optional. To remove attachments, include the existing array of attachment objects, excluding any that you wish to remove.

Note that in most cases the API does not currently return an error code for failed attachment object creation given attachment uploading happens in an asynchronous manner, such cases will manifest with the attachment object either being cleared from the cell or persisted with generated URLs that return error responses when queried. If the same attachment URL fails to upload multiple times in a short time interval then * the API may return an ATTACHMENTS_FAILED_UPLOADING error code in the details field of the response and the attachment object will * be cleared from the cell synchronously.

We also require URLs used to upload have the https:// or http:// protocol (Note: http:// support will be removed in the near future), have a limit of 3 max redirects, and a file size limit of 1GB. In addition, URLs must be publicly accessible, in cases where cookie authentication or logging in to access the file is required, the login page HTML will be downloaded instead of the file.

If too many attachments are uploaded within a short period of time, the server may return a partial failure on record creation with an "Attachment Upload Rate Too High" error.

To link to new records in Gig Payment, event, Attribution, Options, Totals, Performers, Song Choices, Must-have song Choices, Avoid playing, Set List Items, Rehearsal and Totals 2, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

To select new options in song, add new option names to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing option names that you wish to retain. To deselect options, include the existing array of option names, excluding any that you wish to deselect.

Venue, Timings, Contact Number (on the day), First Dance/Song Request (if required), Parking Info, Client Notes, Internal notes, Playlist, Meal details, End of the night and payment notes may contain "mention tokens". A mention token corresponds to a "@mention" in Airtable's user interface; here in the API it will look like <airtable:mention id="menE1i9oBaGX3DseR">@Alex</airtable:mention>. Mention tokens cannot be created via this API and should be left intact (or wholly removed) when updating long text fields.

Values for Name, Performer Fee (actual), GOTO emails, Profit (theoretical), Profit (theoretical/current), Balance Amount, Amount Paid (Turnover), Amount Paid (current), options_ids, Options Price, Options Fees, Description (from event), Early Arrival Price, Late Finish Price, Subtotal, Discount Applied, Date (from event), Total Due (calculated), Deposit Due (Calculated), Profit (projected), Profit (Pot), is_done, Name (from Performers), fillout - song selection, Formatted Date, _has_band?, _has_video, _has_photo, _has_dj, set list (favourites), set list (must-play), set list (avoid), amount (from Gig Payment), _quote_options, Quote, Karaoke (cost), Songs (from Set List Items), Set List Duration (seconds), Set List Total Duration, set list built (copyable), fillout - gig details, GOTO interface, Profit (current) and Profit (theoretical/pot) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

Delete Gigs records
To delete Gigs records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gigs').destroy(['recHk3FbcTQHAvU2v', 'rec99HxggQ2jhscuk'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List Services records
To list records in Services, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Price (to client), pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Price (to client)"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldF6DjfY9EbxkYMB", "fldA5Um7fbE4VFJke"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Services table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Services').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved Singing Waiting - After Dessert (Duet)
Retrieved Singing Waiting - After Dessert (Trio)
Retrieved Acoustic - 1 piece - Guitar or Piano - Ceremony and Reception
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Services').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Services').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Services record
To retrieve an existing record in Services table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Services').find('recJnmxlAvv0tqKZX', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recJnmxlAvv0tqKZX
Create Services records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

Values for Total Fees, Profit Margin, no of gigs, record_id and quote are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

Update Services records
To update Services records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Services records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To link to new records in Gigs, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

Values for Total Fees, Profit Margin, no of gigs, record_id and quote are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

Delete Services records
To delete Services records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Services').destroy(['recJnmxlAvv0tqKZX', 'reco98X0OlFSbNU1W'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List Expenses records
To list records in Expenses, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Date, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Date"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldXXA3ONdcc3eWqX", "fldBmSqX9bK38OLVn"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Expenses table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Expenses').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved Squarespace
Retrieved Scott Bathgate - mixing
Retrieved Logo
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Expenses').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Expenses').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Expenses record
To retrieve an existing record in Expenses table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

In attachment objects included in the retrieved record (Invoice/Receipt/Other), only id, url, and filename are always returned. Other attachment properties may not be included. Note: Attachment URLs returned will expire 2 hours after being returned from our API. If you want to persist the attachments, we recommend downloading them instead of saving the URL. See our support article for more information.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Expenses').find('rec1YG6MgCitUzTOP', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved rec1YG6MgCitUzTOP
Create Expenses records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

To create new attachments in Invoice/Receipt/Other, set the field value to an array of attachment objects. When creating an attachment, url is required, and filename is optional. Airtable will download the file at the given url and keep its own copy of it. All other attachment object properties will be generated server-side soon afterward.

Note that in most cases the API does not currently return an error code for failed attachment object creation given attachment uploading happens in an asynchronous manner, such cases will manifest with the attachment object either being cleared from the cell or persisted with generated URLs that return error responses when queried. If the same attachment URL fails to upload multiple times in a short time interval then * the API may return an ATTACHMENTS_FAILED_UPLOADING error code in the details field of the response and the attachment object will * be cleared from the cell synchronously.

We also require URLs used to upload have the https:// or http:// protocol (Note: http:// support will be removed in the near future), have a limit of 3 max redirects, and a file size limit of 1GB. In addition, URLs must be publicly accessible, in cases where cookie authentication or logging in to access the file is required, the login page HTML will be downloaded instead of the file.

Attachment URLs returned will expire 2 hours after being returned from our API. If you want to persist the attachments, we recommend downloading them instead of saving the URL.

If too many attachments are uploaded within a short period of time, the server may return a partial failure on record creation with an "Attachment Upload Rate Too High" error. See our support article for more information.

Values for Name, Created and Name (from Recipient) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Expenses').create([
  {
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-01-01",
      "Reference": "Squarespace",
      "Cost": 340,
      "Totals": [
        "recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ"
      ],
      "Paid for by": "Scott"
    }
  },
  {
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-01-01",
      "Recipient": "Scott Bathgate",
      "Reference": "mixing",
      "Cost": 625,
      "Totals": [
        "recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ"
      ],
      "Paid for by": "Scott"
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function (record) {
    console.log(record.getId());
  });
});
Output
rec1YG6MgCitUzTOP
recWvwsybufTVaGhU
Update Expenses records
To update Expenses records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Expenses records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To add attachments to Invoice/Receipt/Other, add new attachment objects to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing attachment objects that you wish to retain, to keep preexisting attachments providing id is required (which can be retrieved using the retrieve endpoint), other fields are ignored. For the new attachments being added, url is required, and filename is optional. To remove attachments, include the existing array of attachment objects, excluding any that you wish to remove.

Note that in most cases the API does not currently return an error code for failed attachment object creation given attachment uploading happens in an asynchronous manner, such cases will manifest with the attachment object either being cleared from the cell or persisted with generated URLs that return error responses when queried. If the same attachment URL fails to upload multiple times in a short time interval then * the API may return an ATTACHMENTS_FAILED_UPLOADING error code in the details field of the response and the attachment object will * be cleared from the cell synchronously.

We also require URLs used to upload have the https:// or http:// protocol (Note: http:// support will be removed in the near future), have a limit of 3 max redirects, and a file size limit of 1GB. In addition, URLs must be publicly accessible, in cases where cookie authentication or logging in to access the file is required, the login page HTML will be downloaded instead of the file.

If too many attachments are uploaded within a short period of time, the server may return a partial failure on record creation with an "Attachment Upload Rate Too High" error.

To link to new records in Totals, Showcases and Rehearsal, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

Values for Name, Created and Name (from Recipient) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Expenses').update([
  {
    "id": "rec1YG6MgCitUzTOP",
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-01-01",
      "Reference": "Squarespace",
      "Cost": 340,
      "Totals": [
        "recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ"
      ],
      "Paid for by": "Scott"
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "recWvwsybufTVaGhU",
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-01-01",
      "Recipient": "Scott Bathgate",
      "Reference": "mixing",
      "Cost": 625,
      "Totals": [
        "recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ"
      ],
      "Paid for by": "Scott"
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "rec9tuqaf5kl2YyqM",
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-01-01",
      "Reference": "Logo",
      "Cost": 350,
      "Totals": [
        "recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ"
      ],
      "Paid for by": "Scott"
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function(record) {
    console.log(record.get('Name'));
  });
});
Output


Delete Expenses records
To delete Expenses records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Expenses').destroy(['rec1YG6MgCitUzTOP', 'recWvwsybufTVaGhU'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List People records
To list records in People, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Gigs, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Gigs"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldVA2OWyEdG5oJja", "fldtiOiPUDfq3udTc"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the People table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('People').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved Scott Bruce
Retrieved Katie Lindsay
Retrieved Louise Grant
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('People').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('People').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a People record
To retrieve an existing record in People table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('People').find('recrcRCn2wnq0yv48', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recrcRCn2wnq0yv48
Create People records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

Values for Songs (from Set List Items) (from Gigs), # Gigs, No of Showcases, # Gigs Future, amount Rollup (from Gig Payment copy) and gigs paid are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('People').create([

Update People records
To update People records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on People records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To link to new records in Gigs, Showcases, Gig Payment and Showcase Payment, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

To select new options in roles, add new option names to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing option names that you wish to retain. To deselect options, include the existing array of option names, excluding any that you wish to deselect.

sample of playing may contain "mention tokens". A mention token corresponds to a "@mention" in Airtable's user interface; here in the API it will look like <airtable:mention id="menE1i9oBaGX3DseR">@Alex</airtable:mention>. Mention tokens cannot be created via this API and should be left intact (or wholly removed) when updating long text fields.

Values for Songs (from Set List Items) (from Gigs), # Gigs, No of Showcases, # Gigs Future, amount Rollup (from Gig Payment copy) and gigs paid are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

Delete People records
To delete People records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('People').destroy(['recrcRCn2wnq0yv48', 'recb1UoPng4CdvO8P'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records
Recipient Table
The id for Recipient is tblIgNPC0L10PhpMl. Table ids and table names can be used interchangeably in API requests. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

Field names and field ids can be used interchangeably. Using field ids means field name changes do not require modifications to your API request. We recommend using field ids over field names where possible, to reduce modifications to your API request if the user changes the field name later.

List Recipient records
To list records in Recipient, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Expenses, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Expenses"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldgiRASjrQDfKsQB", "fld4Jnc45L7Z5U1lV"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Recipient table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Recipient').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved MARK MORROW
Retrieved COLIN SNEDDON
Retrieved STARK AGENCY LTD
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Recipient').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Recipient').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Recipient record
To retrieve an existing record in Recipient table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Recipient').find('rec8MEk6Qgmyuhuea', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved rec8MEk6Qgmyuhuea
Create Recipient records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Recipient').create([
  {
    "fields": {
      "Name": "MARK MORROW",
      "Expenses": "MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW",
      "Expenses copy": "MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW"
    }
  },
  {
    "fields": {
      "Name": "COLIN SNEDDON",
      "Expenses": "COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON",
      "Expenses copy": "COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON"
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function (record) {
    console.log(record.getId());
  });
});
Output
rec8MEk6Qgmyuhuea
rec8w5W0WTKbVLS0l
Update Recipient records
To update Recipient records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Recipient records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
Bank Details may contain "mention tokens". A mention token corresponds to a "@mention" in Airtable's user interface; here in the API it will look like <airtable:mention id="menE1i9oBaGX3DseR">@Alex</airtable:mention>. Mention tokens cannot be created via this API and should be left intact (or wholly removed) when updating long text fields.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');

  {

    "fields": {
      "Name": "MARK MORROW",
      "Expenses": "MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW",
      "Expenses copy": "MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW, MARK MORROW"
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "rec8w5W0WTKbVLS0l",
    "fields": {
      "Name": "COLIN SNEDDON",
      "Expenses": "COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON",
      "Expenses copy": "COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON, COLIN SNEDDON"
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "rec61jbfxs14jMrin",
    "fields": {
      "Name": "STARK AGENCY LTD",
      "Expenses": "STARK AGENCY LTD, STARK AGENCY LTD, STARK AGENCY LTD - magazine thing, STARK AGENCY LTD - Three showcases, \"STARK AGENCY LTD - Hamden, Dumfries, Ayrsh...",
      "Expenses copy": "STARK AGENCY LTD, STARK AGENCY LTD, STARK AGENCY LTD - magazine thing, STARK AGENCY LTD - Three showcases, \"STARK AGENCY LTD - Hamden, Dumfries, Ayrsh..."
    }

], function(err, records) {

Delete Recipient records
To delete Recipient records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Recipient').destroy(['rec8MEk6Qgmyuhuea', 'rec8w5W0WTKbVLS0l'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List To Do records
To list records in To Do, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Task and State, pass in:

fields: ["Task", "State"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldds7PsczyGXVFoz", "fldMrp0Kg3VhsUIkL"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Task isn't empty, pass in NOT({Task} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Task} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Task in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Task
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Task in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Task", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the To Do table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.
