List Totals records
To list records in Totals, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Gigs, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Gigs"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fld3vYkSgg3peblyR", "fldHlBv620mBlCAZo"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Totals table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Totals').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved Total
Retrieved 2024
Retrieved 2025
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Totals').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Totals').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Totals record
To retrieve an existing record in Totals table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Totals').find('recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ
Create Totals records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

Values for Gig Turnover (Pot), Gig Turnover (current), Gig Profits (Pot), Gig Profits (Current), Gig Profits(Theoretical), Gig Profit (theoretical/pot), expenses Scott, expenses Garry, Expenses (other), Gig Fees, Showcase Fees, Total Expenses, Total Pot, Total Profit, Total Profit (theoretical), Total Pot (theoretical), Profit (projected) Rollup (from Gigs), No of gigs booked, No of gigs performed, Drawings (Scott), Expenses + Drawings, Gig Profits (Pot) - Drawings, Gig Profits (Current) - Drawings, Gig Profits (Theoretical) - Drawings, Total Pot - Drawings, Total Profit - Drawings, Total Profit (Theoretical) - Drawings, Total Pot (Theoretical) - Drawings and id are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

Update Totals records
To update Totals records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Totals records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To link to new records in Gigs, Expenses, Gigs 2 and Showcase Payment 2, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

Values for Gig Turnover (Pot), Gig Turnover (current), Gig Profits (Pot), Gig Profits (Current), Gig Profits(Theoretical), Gig Profit (theoretical/pot), expenses Scott, expenses Garry, Expenses (other), Gig Fees, Showcase Fees, Total Expenses, Total Pot, Total Profit, Total Profit (theoretical), Total Pot (theoretical), Profit (projected) Rollup (from Gigs), No of gigs booked, No of gigs performed, Drawings (Scott), Expenses + Drawings, Gig Profits (Pot) - Drawings, Gig Profits (Current) - Drawings, Gig Profits (Theoretical) - Drawings, Total Pot - Drawings, Total Profit - Drawings, Total Profit (Theoretical) - Drawings, Total Pot (Theoretical) - Drawings and id are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

Delete Totals records
To delete Totals records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Totals').destroy(['recruuTrjJzTlgAoZ', 'rec9lNhnSLof4eLW0'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output

List Enquiries records
To list records in Enquiries, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Formula and First Name, pass in:

fields: ["Formula", "First Name"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldV5sFOrSoHIsJuM", "fldzRGYFROWja1nPy"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Formula isn't empty, pass in NOT({Formula} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Formula} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Formula in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Formula
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Formula in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Formula", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Enquiries table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Enquiries').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Formula'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved Laura Paterson - 
Retrieved Laura Stewart - 
Retrieved Chloe Jones - 
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Enquiries').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Formula'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Enquiries').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Enquiries record
To retrieve an existing record in Enquiries table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Enquiries').find('recygrGIomDYS15nH', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recygrGIomDYS15nH
Create Enquiries records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

Values for Formula and Full Name are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Enquiries').create([
  {
    "fields": {
      "First Name": "Laura",
      "Last Name": "Paterson",
      "Email": "Lauraepaterson@hotmail.co.uk",
      "Venue Location": "Dundee",
      "Services": "Singing Waiting",
      "Event": "Dundee Showcase"
    }
  },
  {
    "fields": {
      "First Name": "Laura",
      "Last Name": "Stewart",
      "Email": "Laurajanestewart93@gmail.com",
      "Services": "Live Band (3/5/7 piece), Wedding Film, Karaoke/Bandeoke",
      "Event": "Dundee Showcase"
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function (record) {
    console.log(record.getId());
  });
});
Output
recygrGIomDYS15nH
recgoPmwfuzNT1Bt8
Update Enquiries records
To update Enquiries records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Enquiries records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
Message (optional) may contain "mention tokens". A mention token corresponds to a "@mention" in Airtable's user interface; here in the API it will look like <airtable:mention id="menE1i9oBaGX3DseR">@Alex</airtable:mention>. Mention tokens cannot be created via this API and should be left intact (or wholly removed) when updating long text fields.

Values for Formula and Full Name are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Enquiries').update([
  {
    "id": "recygrGIomDYS15nH",
    "fields": {
      "First Name": "Laura",
      "Last Name": "Paterson",
      "Email": "Lauraepaterson@hotmail.co.uk",
      "Venue Location": "Dundee",
      "Services": "Singing Waiting",
      "Event": "Dundee Showcase"
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "recgoPmwfuzNT1Bt8",
    "fields": {
      "First Name": "Laura",
      "Last Name": "Stewart",
      "Email": "Laurajanestewart93@gmail.com",
      "Services": "Live Band (3/5/7 piece), Wedding Film, Karaoke/Bandeoke",
      "Event": "Dundee Showcase"
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "recuYFFWV5nDblnbx",
    "fields": {
      "First Name": "Chloe",
      "Last Name": "Jones",
      "Email": "chloe3110@hotmail.com",
      "phone": "07508631106",
      "Services": "Wedding Film, Photography",
      "Event": "Dundee Showcase"
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function(record) {
    console.log(record.get('Formula'));
  });
});

Delete Enquiries records
To delete Enquiries records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Enquiries').destroy(['recygrGIomDYS15nH', 'recgoPmwfuzNT1Bt8'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Event').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved Showcase - 14/10/23
Retrieved Showcase - 29/10/23
Retrieved Showcase - 12/11/23
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Event').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Event').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Event record
To retrieve an existing record in Event table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Event').find('recJBBxBbKZjHGQ5D', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recJBBxBbKZjHGQ5D
Create Event records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

When creating date time values in Date, ambiguous string inputs like "2020-09-05T07:00:00" and "2020-09-08" will be interpreted according to the time zone of the field if specified, and nonambiguous string inputs with zone offset like "2020-09-05T07:00:00.000Z" and "2020-09-08T00:00:00-07:00" will be interpreted as the underlying timestamp.

Values for Name, description, gig description, description (from Gigs), Venue (from Gigs), Client Name(s) (from Gigs), rehearsal description, Nickname (from showcase), Date (from showcase), Showcase description and Date (from gig (if rehearsal)) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Event').create([
  {
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-10-14T00:00:00.000Z",
      "Type": "Showcase",
      "showcase": [
        "recDuQQfeV0Dheu9Q"
      ]
    }
  },
  {
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-10-29T00:00:00.000Z",
      "Type": "Showcase",
      "showcase": [
        "recNUKRdTFTTq5cqa"
      ]
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function (record) {
    console.log(record.getId());
  });
});
Output
recJBBxBbKZjHGQ5D
recQ18vo2WHgqdJO0
Update Event records
To update Event records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Event records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To link to new records in Gigs, showcase and Rehearsal, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

When updating date time values in Date, ambiguous string inputs like "2020-09-05T07:00:00" and "2020-09-08" will be interpreted according to the time zone of the field if specified, and nonambiguous string inputs with zone offset like "2020-09-05T07:00:00.000Z" and "2020-09-08T00:00:00-07:00" will be interpreted as the underlying timestamp.

Values for Name, description, gig description, description (from Gigs), Venue (from Gigs), Client Name(s) (from Gigs), rehearsal description, Nickname (from showcase), Date (from showcase), Showcase description and Date (from gig (if rehearsal)) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Event').update([
  {
    "id": "recJBBxBbKZjHGQ5D",
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-10-14T00:00:00.000Z",
      "Type": "Showcase",
      "showcase": [
        "recDuQQfeV0Dheu9Q"
      ]
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "recQ18vo2WHgqdJO0",
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-10-29T00:00:00.000Z",
      "Type": "Showcase",
      "showcase": [
        "recNUKRdTFTTq5cqa"
      ]
    }
  },
  {
    "id": "recR50wOUF0EGxIkS",
    "fields": {
      "Date": "2023-11-12T00:00:00.000Z",
      "Type": "Showcase",
      "showcase": [
        "recNiqAH5SSTRWBC9"
      ]
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function(record) {
    console.log(record.get('Name'));
  });
});
Output


Delete Event records
To delete Event records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Event').destroy(['recJBBxBbKZjHGQ5D', 'recQ18vo2WHgqdJO0'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List Songs records
To list records in Songs, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Title, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Title"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldTtEgXOPILozXp8", "fldNrjJvObF3hoO3G"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Songs table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Songs').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved About Damn time - Lizzo
Retrieved Shut up and Dance - Walk The Moon
Retrieved Juice - Lizzo
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Songs').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Songs').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Songs record
To retrieve an existing record in Songs table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Songs').find('recE8bkgnydVmFVtO', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved recE8bkgnydVmFVtO
Create Songs records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

Values for Name, Times requested, set list name, Name (from Performers) (from Gigs) (from Set List Items), Performers (from Gigs) (from Set List Items), duration, record_ id, Performers (from Gigs) Rollup (from Set List Items) and Performed By are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Songs').create([
  {
    "fields": {
      "Title": "About Damn time",
      "Artist": "Lizzo",
      "Genre": "Pop (80s/90’s/Modern)",
      "Gigs": [

Update Songs records
To update Songs records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Songs records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To link to new records in Gigs, Gigs 2, Gigs 3 and Set List Items, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

Values for Name, Times requested, set list name, Name (from Performers) (from Gigs) (from Set List Items), Performers (from Gigs) (from Set List Items), duration, record_ id, Performers (from Gigs) Rollup (from Set List Items) and Performed By are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Songs').update([

Delete Songs records
To delete Songs records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Songs').destroy(['recE8bkgnydVmFVtO', 'recLXVpmCwgWXS7V2'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List Gig Payment records
To list records in Gig Payment, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and person, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "person"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fld32CTpN7rkTMdoJ", "fldVC81qdEnvC43zK"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Gig Payment table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gig Payment').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Play:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Play"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved 25-05-31 - Katie Lindsay
Retrieved 24-12-14 - Katie Wills
Retrieved 25-05-17 - Katie Wills
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Gig Payment').select({
    view: 'Play'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Gig Payment').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Gig Payment record
To retrieve an existing record in Gig Payment table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gig Payment').find('recF7WBv8R7bzfTIN', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});

Create Gig Payment records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

Values for Name, Gig Date, Gigs (from person), Name (from person) and Invoice (from Invoices) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gig Payment').create([
  {
    "fields": {
      "person": [
        "recb1UoPng4CdvO8P"
      ],
      "Gig": [
        "recYkKtlK6nMIb9CE"
      ],
      "Invoices": [
        "recg41t8cdb3fB7cM"
      ],
      "amount": 275
    }
  },
  {
    "fields": {
      "person": [
        "recnKKUTtzQD6OUTu"
      ],
      "Gig": [
        "recR4c0BKY5FWkHmy"
      ],
      "Invoices": [
        "recm8QGfNhRM32c7C"
      ],
      "amount": 250
    }
  }
], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  records.forEach(function (record) {
    console.log(record.getId());
  });
});
Output
recF7WBv8R7bzfTIN
recNcUruh9f49CYTw
Update Gig Payment records
To update Gig Payment records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Gig Payment records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To link to new records in person, Gig and Invoices, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

notes may contain "mention tokens". A mention token corresponds to a "@mention" in Airtable's user interface; here in the API it will look like <airtable:mention id="menE1i9oBaGX3DseR">@Alex</airtable:mention>. Mention tokens cannot be created via this API and should be left intact (or wholly removed) when updating long text fields.

Values for Name, Gig Date, Gigs (from person), Name (from person) and Invoice (from Invoices) are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');

base('Gig Payment').update([

Delete Gig Payment records
To delete Gig Payment records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Gig Payment').destroy(['recF7WBv8R7bzfTIN', 'recNcUruh9f49CYTw'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records

List Invoices records
To list records in Invoices, use the select method.

select returns a query object. To fetch the records matching that query, use the eachPage or firstPage method of the query object.

Returned records do not include any fields with "empty" values, e.g. "", [], or false.

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

You can use the following parameters to filter, sort, and format the results:

fields
array of strings
optional
Only data for fields whose names are in this list will be included in the result. If you don't need every field, you can use this parameter to reduce the amount of data transferred.

For example, to only return data from Name and Date, pass in:

fields: ["Name", "Date"]
You can also perform the same action with field ids (they can be found in the fields section):

fields: ["fldgHFcQ6Wp4ffk87", "fldtScQvrXDbdQNnB"]
filterByFormula
string
optional
A formula used to filter records. The formula will be evaluated for each record, and if the result is not 0, false, "", NaN, [], or #Error! the record will be included in the response. We recommend testing your formula in the Formula field UI before using it in your API request.

If combined with the view parameter, only records in that view which satisfy the formula will be returned.

The formula must be encoded first before passing it as a value. You can use this tool to not only encode the formula but also create the entire url you need. For example, to only include records where Name isn't empty, pass in NOT({Name} = '') as a parameter like this:

filterByFormula: "NOT({Name} = '')"

Note: Airtable's API only accepts request with a URL shorter than 16,000 characters. Encoded formulas may cause your requests to exceed this limit. To fix this issue you can instead make a POST request to /v0/{baseId}/{tableIdOrName}/listRecords while passing the parameters within the body of the request instead of the query parameters. See our support article on this for more information.

maxRecords
number
optional
The maximum total number of records that will be returned in your requests. If this value is larger than pageSize (which is 100 by default), you may have to load multiple pages to reach this total. See the Pagination section below for more.pageSize
number
optional
The number of records returned in each request. Must be less than or equal to 100. Default is 100. See the Pagination section below for more.sort
array of objects
optional
A list of sort objects that specifies how the records will be ordered. Each sort object must have a field key specifying the name of the field to sort on, and an optional direction key that is either "asc" or "desc". The default direction is "asc".

The sort parameter overrides the sorting of the view specified in the view parameter. If neither the sort nor the view parameter is included, the order of records is arbitrary.

For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, send these two query parameters:

sort%5B0%5D%5Bfield%5D=Name
sort%5B0%5D%5Bdirection%5D=desc
For example, to sort records by Name in descending order, pass in:

[{field: "Name", direction: "desc"}]
view
string
optional
The name or ID of a view in the Invoices table. If set, only the records in that view will be returned. The records will be sorted according to the order of the view unless the sort parameter is included, which overrides that order. Fields hidden in this view will be returned in the results. To only return a subset of fields, use the fields parameter.cellFormat
string
optional
The format that should be used for cell values. Supported values are:

json: cells will be formatted as JSON, depending on the field type.

string: cells will be formatted as user-facing strings, regardless of the field type. The timeZone and userLocale parameters are required when using string as the cellFormat.

Note: You should not rely on the format of these strings, as it is subject to change.
The default is json.

timeZone
string
optional
The time zone that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

userLocale
string
optional
The user locale that should be used to format dates when using string as the cellFormat. This parameter is required when using string as the cellFormat.

returnFieldsByFieldId
boolean
optional
An optional boolean value that lets you return field objects where the key is the field id.

This defaults to false, which returns field objects where the key is the field name.

recordMetadata
array of strings
optional
An optional field that, if includes commentCount, adds a commentCount read only property on each record returned.

Pagination
The server returns one page of records at a time. Each page will contain pageSize records, which is 100 by default.

To fetch the next page of records, call fetchNextPage.

Pagination will stop when you've reached the end of your table. If the maxRecords parameter is passed, pagination will stop once you've reached this maximum.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Invoices').select({
    // Selecting the first 3 records in Grid view:
    maxRecords: 3,
    view: "Grid view"
}).eachPage(function page(records, fetchNextPage) {
    // This function (`page`) will get called for each page of records.

    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });

    // To fetch the next page of records, call `fetchNextPage`.
    // If there are more records, `page` will get called again.
    // If there are no more records, `done` will get called.
    fetchNextPage();

}, function done(err) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
});
Output
Retrieved 1
Retrieved 2
Retrieved 3
Fetch first page
// If you only want the first page of records, you can
// use `firstPage` instead of `eachPage`.
base('Invoices').select({
    view: 'Grid view'
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved', record.get('Name'));
    });
});
Fetch additional record metadata
// If you want to fetch the number of comments for each record,
// include the `recordMetadata` param.
base('Invoices').select({
    recordMetadata: ['commentCount']
}).firstPage(function(err, records) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    records.forEach(function(record) {
        console.log('Retrieved a record with', record.commentCount, 'comments');
    });
});
 
Iteration may timeout due to client inactivity or server restarts. In that case, the client will receive a 422 response with error message LIST_RECORDS_ITERATOR_NOT_AVAILABLE. It may then restart iteration from the beginning.

 
Retrieve a Invoices record
To retrieve an existing record in Invoices table, use the find method.

Any "empty" fields (e.g. "", [], or false) in the record will not be returned.

In attachment objects included in the retrieved record (Invoice), only id, url, and filename are always returned. Other attachment properties may not be included. Note: Attachment URLs returned will expire 2 hours after being returned from our API. If you want to persist the attachments, we recommend downloading them instead of saving the URL. See our support article for more information.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Invoices').find('rec1LEf6bxsdmTs7Y', function(err, record) {
    if (err) { console.error(err); return; }
    console.log('Retrieved', record.id);
});
Output
Retrieved rec1LEf6bxsdmTs7Y
Create Invoices records
To create new records, use the create method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have one key whose value is an inner object containing your record's cell values, keyed by either field name or field id.

Returns an array of record objects created if the call succeeded, including record IDs which will uniquely identify the records within Every Angle.

To create new attachments in Invoice, set the field value to an array of attachment objects. When creating an attachment, url is required, and filename is optional. Airtable will download the file at the given url and keep its own copy of it. All other attachment object properties will be generated server-side soon afterward.

Note that in most cases the API does not currently return an error code for failed attachment object creation given attachment uploading happens in an asynchronous manner, such cases will manifest with the attachment object either being cleared from the cell or persisted with generated URLs that return error responses when queried. If the same attachment URL fails to upload multiple times in a short time interval then * the API may return an ATTACHMENTS_FAILED_UPLOADING error code in the details field of the response and the attachment object will * be cleared from the cell synchronously.

We also require URLs used to upload have the https:// or http:// protocol (Note: http:// support will be removed in the near future), have a limit of 3 max redirects, and a file size limit of 1GB. In addition, URLs must be publicly accessible, in cases where cookie authentication or logging in to access the file is required, the login page HTML will be downloaded instead of the file.

Attachment URLs returned will expire 2 hours after being returned from our API. If you want to persist the attachments, we recommend downloading them instead of saving the URL.

If too many attachments are uploaded within a short period of time, the server may return a partial failure on record creation with an "Attachment Upload Rate Too High" error. See our support article for more information.

Values for Name, invoice file name and Created are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly created.

The Airtable API will perform best-effort automatic data conversion from string values if the typecast parameter is passed in (click to show example). Automatic conversion is disabled by default to ensure data integrity, but it may be helpful for integrating with 3rd party data sources.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

], function(err, records) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;

Update Invoices records
To update Invoices records, use the update or replace method. An update will only update the fields you include. Fields not included will be unchanged. A replace will perform a destructive update and clear all unincluded cell values. A replace call on Invoices records will always fail. The example at the right uses the non-destructive update method. Click here to show a destructive replace call.
The first argument should be an array of up to 10 record objects. Each of these objects should have an id property representing the record ID and a fields property which contains all of your record's cell values by field name or field id for all of your record's cell values by field name.
To add attachments to Invoice, add new attachment objects to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing attachment objects that you wish to retain, to keep preexisting attachments providing id is required (which can be retrieved using the retrieve endpoint), other fields are ignored. For the new attachments being added, url is required, and filename is optional. To remove attachments, include the existing array of attachment objects, excluding any that you wish to remove.

Note that in most cases the API does not currently return an error code for failed attachment object creation given attachment uploading happens in an asynchronous manner, such cases will manifest with the attachment object either being cleared from the cell or persisted with generated URLs that return error responses when queried. If the same attachment URL fails to upload multiple times in a short time interval then * the API may return an ATTACHMENTS_FAILED_UPLOADING error code in the details field of the response and the attachment object will * be cleared from the cell synchronously.

We also require URLs used to upload have the https:// or http:// protocol (Note: http:// support will be removed in the near future), have a limit of 3 max redirects, and a file size limit of 1GB. In addition, URLs must be publicly accessible, in cases where cookie authentication or logging in to access the file is required, the login page HTML will be downloaded instead of the file.

If too many attachments are uploaded within a short period of time, the server may return a partial failure on record creation with an "Attachment Upload Rate Too High" error.

To link to new records in Gig Payment and Showcase `payment, add new linked record IDs to the existing array. Be sure to include all existing linked record IDs that you wish to retain. To unlink records, include the existing array of record IDs, excluding any that you wish to unlink.

Values for Name, invoice file name and Created are automatically computed by Airtable and cannot be directly updated. You cannot clear these, even with a replace call.

Automatic data conversion for update actions can be enabled via typecast parameter. See create record for details.

You can also include a single record object at the top level. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Invoices').update([
  {
    "id": "rec1LEf6bxsdmTs7Y",

      "Date": "2025-05-03",

          "id": "attT2rpuSWNmB3zSC"

Delete Invoices records
To delete Invoices records, use the destroy method. Note that table names and table ids can be used interchangeably. Using table ids means table name changes do not require modifications to your API request.

The first parameter to destroy is an array of up to 10 record IDs to delete.

You can also set the first parameter to a record ID to delete a single record. Click here to show an example.

 
Code
var Airtable = require('airtable');
var base = new Airtable({apiKey: 'YOUR_SECRET_API_TOKEN'}).base('appZXteLrpESv7H8X');

base('Invoices').destroy(['rec1LEf6bxsdmTs7Y', 'recg41t8cdb3fB7cM'], function(err, deletedRecords) {
  if (err) {
    console.error(err);
    return;
  }
  console.log('Deleted', deletedRecords.length, 'records');
});
Output
Deleted 2 records
